## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically includes a restoring force (function of x), damping (function of v), and possibly external/parametric driving (function of t). Nonlinear terms involve powers of x, v, or their products.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (nonlinear coupling term)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * v (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Helmholtz-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric potential with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x**2) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Products x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol type self-excitation
- Trigonometric functions of t (sin/cos) → external periodic driving forces or parametric excitation
- Cubic position terms x**3 → Duffing-type hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring
- Odd powers of velocity (v**3) → nonlinear drag forces common in Rayleigh-type dissipation
- Product of x and trigonometric function of t → parametric resonance where stiffness varies periodically
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Ratio of polynomial in x over polynomial in x → bounded restoring force that saturates at large displacement

# Analysis of Candidate Formulas vs Ground Truth

## Ground Truth (GT):
```
-0.0907*v**3 - 0.5945*v*exp(-|v|) - 2.9429*x**3 + 0.5691*sin(t)
```

The key terms are:
1. `sin(t)` — sinusoidal in t with frequency 1
2. `v**3` — cubic in velocity
3. `v*exp(-|v|)` — velocity times exponential of absolute velocity (NOT a polynomial term)
4. `x**3` — cubic in position

The critical term is `v*exp(-|v|)`. This is a nonlinear, non-polynomial function of v that involves the absolute value. None of the candidate formulas can replicate this term unless they contain `exp()` with `|v|` or equivalent.

## Systematic Check

Let me examine each candidate for the presence of `exp(-|v|)` or any exponential term:

**Candidates 1-27, 29-50**: These contain only polynomial terms in x and v, trigonometric functions of t (and sometimes x), and combinations thereof. None contain `exp(-|v|)` or any exponential function of v. Therefore, none of these can match the GT's `v*exp(-|v|)` term.

**Candidate 28**: `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v*x**2 + c3*v + c4*sin(c5 + c6*t) + c7*v**3 + c8*exp(c9*x**2)`

This contains an exponential term `exp(c9*x**2)`, but it's a function of x, not v. The GT requires `v*exp(-|v|)`, which depends on v. This candidate cannot match because:
- The exponential is in x, not v
- There's no |v| dependency
- Even if we tried to approximate, `exp(c9*x**2)` is fundamentally different from `v*exp(-|v|)`

## Detailed consideration of polynomial approximation

Could `v*exp(-|v|)` be exactly represented by polynomial/trigonometric terms? No. The function `v*exp(-|v|)` is an odd function of v that decays exponentially for large |v|. No finite polynomial in v can match this behavior — polynomials grow without bound while `v*exp(-|v|)` → 0 as |v| → ∞. This is a fundamental mathematical impossibility.

Could any `v*cos(c*t)` term substitute? No — `cos(c*t)` depends on t, not v. The GT term `v*exp(-|v|)` depends only on v, not on t or x.

## Conclusion

The GT contains the term `β·v·exp(-|v|)` with β ≈ 0.5945 (non-zero). This is an essential, non-polynomial function of v. None of the 50 candidates contain an exponential function of v (or |v|). The only candidate with any exponential (Candidate 28) has `exp(c9*x**2)`, which depends on x, not v. Therefore, no candidate can be made equivalent to the GT.

**GT:** `-0.0907*v**3 - 0.5945*v*exp(-Abs(v)) - 2.9429*x**3 + 0.5691*sin(t)`

The key terms in GT are:
1. `sin(t)` - sinusoidal in t
2. `x**3` - cubic in x
3. `v**3` - cubic in v
4. `v*exp(-Abs(v))` - this is a special nonlinear function of v

The critical challenge is term 4: `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. This function is NOT a polynomial in v, NOT `v*cos(anything involving t)`, and NOT any simple algebraic combination. Let me analyze what functions the candidates use to approximate this term.

**Key insight:** `v*exp(-Abs(v))` cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials in v (like `v`, `v**2*x`, `v**3`, etc.)
- `v*cos(c*t)` (this depends on t, not v)
- Any finite polynomial combination

Let me check each candidate:

**Candidates with `v*cos(c*t)` terms (1-8, 42-50, etc.):** The term `v*cos(c*t)` depends on both v and t, while `v*exp(-Abs(v))` depends only on v. These are fundamentally different basis functions. Setting `c7=0` would make `cos(c7*t)=1`, giving just a constant times `v`. But `v*exp(-Abs(v))` is not linear in v. So `v*cos(c*t)` cannot match `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

**Candidates with polynomial terms in v only (like `v`, `v**3`, `v**2*x`, etc.):** No finite polynomial can equal `v*exp(-Abs(v))` for all v. This is because `exp(-Abs(v))` is not a polynomial.

**Candidate 28:** Has `exp(c9*x**2)` - this depends on x, not v. Cannot match `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

**Candidate 44:** Has `cos(c9*v*x)` - depends on both v and x, not just v. Cannot match.

**Candidate 50:** Has `sin(c7 + c8*x + c9*t)` - depends on x and t, not matching `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

For ALL candidates, I need to check if any combination of their terms can produce `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. Since `exp(-Abs(v))` is a non-polynomial, non-trigonometric function of v, and none of the candidates contain `exp` terms involving v (or `Abs(v)`), none can exactly reproduce this term.

Let me verify there's no candidate with an exponential in v... Going through all 50 candidates:
- Candidate 28 has `exp(c9*x**2)` - wrong variable
- No other candidate has any `exp` involving `v`
